  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_dbdbdc30-4895-4ff1-a33f-a55874d7a286'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

Batgirl), the Joker kidnaps the commissioner and attacks his mind in </span>
  <span id="freeText6465201308358130688" style="display:none">For the first time the Joker's origin is revealed in this tale of insanity and human perseverance. Looking to prove that any man can be pushed past his breaking point and go mad, the Joker attempts to drive Commissioner Gordon insane. <br /><br />After shooting and permanently paralyzing his daughter Barbara (a.k.a. Batgirl), the Joker kidnaps the commissioner and attacks his mind in hopes of breaking the man. <br /><br />But refusing to give up, Gordon maintains his sanity with the help of Batman in an effort to beset the madman.</span>

<div id="review_1576581082" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1576581082" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1576581082?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=comic-graphic-novel">comic-graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=5-star-reads">5-star-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1576581082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10204924897391512167"><b>“All it takes is one bad day to reduce the sanest man alive to lunacy. That's how far the world is from where I am. Just one bad day.”</b><br/><br/>Now this was good, and I mean good. It’s such a simple idea, but so real and powerful. I mean one bad day is all it takes. One push, one snap, one descent into chaos and it’s over. Once you’ve crossed that threshold then things will never be the same again. And the Joker, being the sly and brilliant villain that he is, wants to share the experience with the world.</span>
  <span id="freeText10204924897391512167" style="display:none"><b>“All it takes is one bad day to reduce the sanest man alive to lunacy. That's how far the world is from where I am. Just one bad day.”</b><br><br>Now this was good, and I mean good. It’s such a simple idea, but so real and powerful. I mean one bad day is all it takes. One push, one snap, one descent into chaos and it’s over. Once you’ve crossed that threshold then things will never be the same again. And the Joker, being the sly and brilliant villain that he is, wants to share the experience with the world. He wants to show humanity that they are not that far from him. The first man he wants to reduce is the stalwart Commissioner Gordon. But, I think we all know who is intended victim actually is. <br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457722511i/18395483._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Joker was once normal. He had a girlfriend; he had a job, but the world shitted on him somewhat chronic. And like many people he was forced to turn to crime; he was forced to break society's rules in order to survive. That’s where it all began. That first step into the darkness led to many other steps down the road of corruption. It wasn’t long before petty crime turned to murder and butchery. The Joker became ruined and lost himself in his nasty deeds. This is a great origin story, one that fully lives up to the character immense personality. Allan More totally nails it. <br><br><b>"THERE IS NO SANITY CLAUSE! <br><br>SO WHEN YOU FIND YOURSELF LOCKED ONTO AN UNPLEASANT TRAIN OF THOUGHT, HEADING FOR THE PLACES IN YOUR PAST WHERE THE SCREAMING IS UNBEARABLE, REMEMBER THERE'S ALWAYS MADNESS. <br><br>MADNESS IS THE EMERGENCY EXIT... <br><br>YOU CAN JUST STEP OUTSIDE, AND CLOSE THE DOOR ON ALL THOSE DREADFUL THINGS THAT HAPPENED. YOU CAN LOCK THEM AWAY... <br><br>FOREVER.”</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457722511i/18395484._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And the ending, it’s all about the ending. The Joker’s personality is infectious. At least, he wants it to be. He’s always tried to bring down the good. He ruined Harvey Dent, and he has always wanted to ruin the bat. And he just may have. The end is suggestive of two things: firstly, Batman strangling the Joker in one final heroic act, there’s some irony in that sentence; secondly, Batman descending to the Jokers level and embracing the insanity of one bad day.<br><br>I'll leave you with this picture and see if you can decide:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457722570i/18395498._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>__________________________________<br><br>You can connect with me on social media via <a href="https://linktr.ee/sean.ultra_vegan1" rel="nofollow noopener">My Linktree</a>.<br>__________________________________</span>
  <a data-text-id="10204924897391512167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2630490099376754611"><b>All it takes is one bad day.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1526670397ra/25563162.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This is one of the most iconic comics in the Batman/Joker mythos and arguably has a place as one of the most iconic comics out there period. I think most people will agree that Bolland's visuals are just unbelievable. The expressions on the faces, the body language, even the colors are as close to perfect as you can get.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1526679188i/25563901._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='600' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>And Moore is at the top of his game here.   <span id="freeText2630490099376754611" style="display:none"><b>All it takes is one bad day.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1526670397ra/25563162.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is one of the most iconic comics in the Batman/Joker mythos and arguably has a place as one of the most iconic comics out there period. I think most people will agree that Bolland's visuals are just unbelievable. The expressions on the faces, the body language, even the colors are as close to perfect as you can get.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1526679188i/25563901._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="600" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And Moore is at the top of his game here. Wow. Just...wow!<br>The ripple effects of what happened here <i>not only</i> created Oracle, but inspired a ton of other great storylines.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1526670996i/25563228._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="600" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I would have thought that a <b>Joker Origin</b> story was maybe the stupidest idea ever before reading this, but I think Moore pulled it off beautifully. Mainly because this had such a wonderful hint of madness to it, that it even with the Joker telling you about his past, it <i>still</i> leaves you wondering if that's <i>really</i> what happened.<br><b>And that ending.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1526670841i/25563203._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Highly recommended.</span>

<div id="review_17784881" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/17784881" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/994396-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442509596p2/994396.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/17784881?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/994396-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Erin by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/313370-zak">Zak</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer17784881&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer17784881" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4043218695614317798">It causes me no joy to give any comic written by Alan Moore one star, but this is how it has to be. Now, before I write a single word more, let me start with this simple disclaimer: I consider Alan Moore the best writer to have ever worked in comics. There are no qualifiers to that; no qualifications. Moore is unmatched.<br/><br/>But The Killing Joke? As a Batman book, it's just bad. That isn't to say there's nothing to like here: this book certainly has its moments; some of which are brilliant, in fact. </span>
  <span id="freeText4043218695614317798" style="display:none">It causes me no joy to give any comic written by Alan Moore one star, but this is how it has to be. Now, before I write a single word more, let me start with this simple disclaimer: I consider Alan Moore the best writer to have ever worked in comics. There are no qualifiers to that; no qualifications. Moore is unmatched.<br /><br />But The Killing Joke? As a Batman book, it's just bad. That isn't to say there's nothing to like here: this book certainly has its moments; some of which are brilliant, in fact. But as a story, it doesn't work.<br /><br />Killing Joke is really two stories told in parallel. It provides an origin for the Joker while simultaneously following him on a scheme to drive Commissioner Gordon insane.<br /><br />The origin is largely based on an old issue of Batman from the 50's: "The Man Behind the Red Hood." As much as I appreciate the nod to the past, the Red Hood origin of the Joker is one I could do without. While I am not in favor of attempts to make Batman "realistic," I do feel that some elements should be handled carefully if handled at all.<br /><br />And that's really the problem here. Not only did Alan Moore use an absurd origin; he made it more so. In the original, the Red Hood was a hardened criminal before he became the Joker. In this version, he was a comedian having a really bad day.<br /><br />I think I understand what Moore was trying to do here. I believe he wanted to create an element of pathos in the Joker's past while playing up the absurdity of the medium.<br /><br />But the result felt sloppy. Instead of adding layers to the Joker's personality, it just made him less interesting.<br /><br />The real problem with Killing Joke, however, is the other story line. The Joker takes Barbara Gordon by surprise, shooting and paralyzing her. Setting aside my personal objection to crippling one of DC's best (and, at the time, few) female characters, Moore missed a huge opportunity here. Had Oracle’s injury been sustained as Batgirl, the psychological effect on Batman could have been developed in great depth, as he’d have been responsible for placing her in harm’s way. As it was, the story only takes a toll on her father, and that's largely wrapped up by the end of the comic.<br /><br />The Joker's motive for all this mayhem, to break Jim Gordon and prove that a bad enough day can drive anyone insane, comes to nothing. In part, he's foiled by Batman, but really he loses because he's wrong: Gordon is strong enough to survive his ordeal.<br /><br />In the end, after everything, The Joker's comprehension of the human psyche is wrong. To me, this destroys the character’s credibility. The Joker has no superpowers, but madness is his expertise. For him to set to prove a point about insanity than fail, not due to Batman but rather his own assumptions, weakens him. Even after shooting Barbara, he ends the book less of a threat than he started.<br /><br />Now, let's be honest: one star is a harsh rating, and were this book not commonly called "The Greatest Batman Story Ever Told" I'd almost certainly have been more lenient. There are certainly excellent aspects to the writing and the art; aspects that would buy any other book three stars.<br /><br />But this isn't any other book. It's one of the most significant Batman stories written, having forever altered the continuity and status of several characters. It's Alan Moore's most famous Batman story.<br /><br />And it really isn't that good.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4043218695614317798" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2307632852?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2307632852" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10707323147288827305">I asked a GR friend: Marvel or DC?<br/><br/>Her response made me think. She said, “Marvel over all. But DC has the better villains.”<br/><br/>Whu - ?<br/><br/>Well.<br/><br/>Yeah, I’ll be damned, I think she’s right.<br/><br/>Looking at all of the Marvel villains, I think maybe only Red Skull or Bullseye come close to matching the lunatic force of DC’s lineup. Magneto and Doctor Doom are powerful and bad, but also have some incongruous redeeming qualities. Lex Luthor, Deathstroke, Brainiac, Bane, Harley Quinn and all the Batman bad guys headlin</span>
  <span id="freeText10707323147288827305" style="display:none">I asked a GR friend: Marvel or DC?<br><br>Her response made me think. She said, “Marvel over all. But DC has the better villains.”<br><br>Whu - ?<br><br>Well.<br><br>Yeah, I’ll be damned, I think she’s right.<br><br>Looking at all of the Marvel villains, I think maybe only Red Skull or Bullseye come close to matching the lunatic force of DC’s lineup. Magneto and Doctor Doom are powerful and bad, but also have some incongruous redeeming qualities. Lex Luthor, Deathstroke, Brainiac, Bane, Harley Quinn and all the Batman bad guys headlined by The Joker are more nefarious, scarier, and just plain bad.<br><br>I think a cogent argument could be made that The Joker is THE comics villain. He’s evil, insane and damn it all interesting as hell.<br><br>Just as Milton’s most enduringly intriguing player is not God or the Archangels but Satan, DC has in The Joker created an enigma (Sorry Riddler) of a criminal source that defies logic and is simply an opposing force for our heroes, motives and reason be damned. The Joker is a personification of the chaos waiting out in the dark beyond the firelight, and his is a blindly malevolent force. As Michael Caine’s Alfred in the 2008 film The Dark Knight said, “some men aren't looking for anything logical, like money. They can't be bought, bullied, reasoned, or negotiated with. Some men just want to watch the world burn.”<br><br>“All it takes is one bad day to reduce the sanest man alive to lunacy. That's how far the world is from where I am. Just one bad day.” <br><br>In his attempt to madden Gordon and lure Batman to his doom, The Joker also provides a tenuous connection to humanity. Just as Shakespeare’s Richard III is all the more terrible because he is a man, so too is The joker all the more villainous because for all his insanity and bad intent, he is one of us and closer than some Melvillian beast or Lovecraftian old god. In the context of the Batman story, the theatrical irony the reader gets is that Joker and Batman are more alike than they realize, both transformed from what they would have been by a traumatic loss.<br><br>Alan Moore and Brian Bolland’s 1988 sympathetic backstory to the Joker’s origin story is a MUST read for Moore fans, Batman devotees and all enthusiasts of the genre. The influence on later comics and even on the films (particularly Tim Burton’s vision) is unmistakable.<br><br>Grim, violent, sometimes difficult to look at, this is nonetheless a graphic novel at the apex of the genus. Moore’s writing is engaging and relentless, Bolland’s art is mesmerizing.<br><br>Highly recommended.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1576159690i/28599821._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="10707323147288827305" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_514420806" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/514420806" />
    <a title="Alejandro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro"><img alt="Alejandro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328672389p2/665584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/514420806?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alejandro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alejandro" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro">Alejandro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=super-heroes">super-heroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=comic-book">comic-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=politics">politics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=detective">detective</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer514420806" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14190045051014122255"><b>
  <u>A truly masterpiece of the comic books!</u>
</b><br/><br/><br/><i>This is a prestige format stand-alone story.</i><br/><br/><br/><u>Creative Team:</u><br/><br/>Writer: Alan Moore<br/><br/>Illustrator: Brian Bolland<br/><br/>Colorist: John Higgins<br/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>HAVE COURAGE</u>
</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>Nothing’s going to be the same… …not ever again.</i>
</b><br/><br/>A writer should have balls, and I don’t mean the organic meat sacs, since a female writer is the same entitled to have balls. But if you aren’t confortable with the “male metaphor”, I am confident that you already got that I am talking about writing with courage.<br/><br/>A </span>
  <span id="freeText14190045051014122255" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>A truly masterpiece of the comic books!</u>
</b><br /><br /><br /><i>This is a prestige format stand-alone story.</i><br /><br /><br /><u>Creative Team:</u><br /><br />Writer: Alan Moore<br /><br />Illustrator: Brian Bolland<br /><br />Colorist: John Higgins<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>HAVE COURAGE</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Nothing’s going to be the same… …not ever again.</i>
</b><br /><br />A writer should have balls, and I don’t mean the organic meat sacs, since a female writer is the same entitled to have balls. But if you aren’t confortable with the “male metaphor”, I am confident that you already got that I am talking about writing with courage.<br /><br />A writer without courage never will be able to impact the readers. <br /><br />Madonna commented many years ago that there is not such thing as bad publicity, that any publicity is good publicity.<br /><br />So, fitting that concept into writing, I think that there isn’t such thing as “bad impact”, that any impact is good impact. Since if people talk about a book, about a story, not matter their intention, the story becomes famous, it provokes curiousity, people got aware of it.<br /><br />Alan Moore never thought that DC Comics would approve his proposal about this Batman’s story involving the crippling of Barbara Gordon. But it was approved by the editorial staff, and a surprised Alan Moore started to write… <b>with courage</b>. <br /><br />I am not insensitive, and I can understand why so many people got angry to the nasty stuff that the character of Barbara Gordon suffered in this story. However, sometimes a bad thing happened for a good reason. <br /><br />Barbara Gordon was Batgirl. But, to be honest, how much difference can she does as such heroine? She was just yet another bat-costumed crime-fighter and trust me, for Batman, that he’s supposed to be a “lonely crusader”, he has too many bat-costumed crime-fighters around. However, due her awful episode in <i>The Killing Joke</i>, Barbara Gordon proved her value as character… proved <b>her courage</b>. <br /><br />Barbara Gordon became a handicapped person, but hardly of disappearing from the pages of comics, she <b>evolved</b> into “Oracle”, and as such persona, she turned to be one of the most powerful characters in the DC Universe. From her wheelchair, using her intelligence, hacking skills and information searches, she became a key ally to not only the Bat-family but also the Titans and even the Justice League.<br /><br />And then… due social pressure from people that never really understood the value of Barbara Gordon, DC Comics devolved her to be Batgirl again. Yipee, hurray (using Droopy’s voice tone). Yet another bat-costumed throwing-batarangs character again, one of many others. All her courage overcoming a monumental tragedy, just erased.<br /><br />And curious that people raged against what Barbara suffered but nobody gave a crap about James Gordon’s own suffering and humiliation, but of course, if you are a heterosexual caucasian man (even if you are an imaginary character reflecting that type of person)… you’re screwed, since nobody will defend your dignity. (and hey, I am a latin man, so since I am part of a “minority” group, if you attack my review, I am in my “right” of accusing you of a racist/ethnic hate act… geez! What a crazy world where we live in!)<br /><br />It seems that villains can do all the harm and killing that they wish, <b>BUT</b> only if they target heterosexual caucasian men, since it seems that any other type of people in this world is under the label of some “minority” group and therefore, there will be rage riots about it.<br /><br />I think that “labels” instead of unite us, they just keep away the distance between each other in this little blue planet. People see me as a heterosexual latin man. And I can’t deny that. That’s what I am in the eyes of society. I born that way…<br /><br />…However, I’d prefer to be a “citizen of the world”. But maybe I am crazy, since it looks like everybody else feels confortable under the safety of their particular sex/ethnic labels.<br /><br />And call me crazy again, but it seems that in real life, criminals just pick any kind of victim, regardless of their sexual preferences or ethnic origins, just watch the news anyday, so I don’t understand why literature should present politically correct villains only.<br /><br />Writers! Don’t lose your courage! It’s not an easy path, but true born writers aren’t meant to travel in safe roads. We, readers, are an unthankful species, we don’t deserve you. However, I hope that you, writers, still being willing to impact us, to make us think, and to provoke us feelings.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>ONE (VERY) BAD DAY</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>How can two people hate so much without knowing each other?</i>
</b><br /><br />Batman is a cause of order. Joker is a force of chaos. Right?<br /><br />Therefore, they are totally different. Right?<br /><br /><b>THAT</b> is <i>the killing joke</i>…<br /><br />…<u>they aren’t that different</u>.<br /><br />One bad day. That was all they needed to get crazy.<br /><br />You may tell me: “Oh! But only Joker is crazy!”. Right. Since disguising as a bat is clearly a sanity’s proof.<br /><br />Joker’s origins are unknown (since you can’t trust what you read in this tale about his past, after all, those are the memories of an insane killer), but you can be sure that something bad, something very bad, happened to him, one day, and the following day, he turned to be The Joker.<br /><br />Bruce Wayne had a bad day, a very bad day, his parents died in front of him while he was still just a defenseless kid, and the following day, he turned to be The Batman (training could take years, but he was The Batman since that moment).<br /><br />The Joker kills people in very theatrical ways.<br /><br />The Batman protects people in very theatrical ways.<br /><br />Gotham City is in the middle…<br /><br />…in the hands of murdering clowns and costumed vigilantes…<br /><br />…in the hands of mad men.<br /><br />The only one that keeps Gotham City from falling deep into madness?<br /><br />James Gordon.<br /><br />The Joker will do everything (and I mean <b>EVERYTHING!</b>) to give to James Gordon, a bad day, a very bad day, and turned him crazy.<br /><br />But that’s not the scariest thing…<br /><br />…oh, no…<br /><br />…that isn’t <i>the killing joke</i>.<br /><br />The scariest thing is when two people, supposed to be opposites…<br /><br />…they laugh for the same joke.<br /><br /><b>BOOM!</b><br /><br />Mic drop, and I’m outta here!<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14190045051014122255" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jon Nakapalau" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jon Nakapalau" href="/user/show/58774673-jon-nakapalau">Jon Nakapalau</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1736085323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18352117428670388688">The best Batman/Joker story ever! Alan Moore asks the question no one else ever wanted to ask: how much of who the Joker is can be attributed to Batman? How much of who Batman is can be attributed to the Joker? 'Primordial Unity' and the 'Tragic Birth' of both the Joker and Batman has never been explored more deeply - I think Nietzsche would have liked this story.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2944544790566534942">Batman: The Killing Joke (Batman), Alan Moore, Brian Bolland (Illustrator), Tim Sale (Introduction)<br/><br/>Batman: The Killing Joke is a 1988 Comic graphic novel featuring the characters Batman and the Joker written by Alan Moore and illustrated by Brian Bolland. The Killing Joke provides an origin story for the super-villain the Joker.<br/><br/>The man who will become the Joker is an unnamed engineer who quits his job at a chemical company to become a stand-up comedian, only to fail miserably. <br/><br/>Desperate to suppo</span>
  <span id="freeText2944544790566534942" style="display:none">Batman: The Killing Joke (Batman), Alan Moore, Brian Bolland (Illustrator), Tim Sale (Introduction)<br /><br />Batman: The Killing Joke is a 1988 Comic graphic novel featuring the characters Batman and the Joker written by Alan Moore and illustrated by Brian Bolland. The Killing Joke provides an origin story for the super-villain the Joker.<br /><br />The man who will become the Joker is an unnamed engineer who quits his job at a chemical company to become a stand-up comedian, only to fail miserably. <br /><br />Desperate to support his pregnant wife Jeannie, he agrees to guide two criminals through the chemical plant where he previously worked so that they can rob the playing card company next to it. During the planning, the police inform him that his wife and unborn child have died in a household accident.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: سال 2005 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: بتمن: شوخی مرگبار؛ نویسنده: آلن مور؛<br /><br />بتمن: شوخی مرگبار، یک رمان گرافیکی از شرکت آمریکایی «دی.‌سی کامیکس» است، که برپایه دو شخصیت «بتمن» و «جوکر» نوشته شده، و نخستین بار در ماه مارس سال 1998میلادی منتشر شده است؛ داستان رمان، توسط «آلن مور» نگاشته شده، و «برایان بالند»، کار تصویرسازی را انجام داده‌ است.؛ در این کامیک، تمرکز اصلی بر روی ریشه ی پیدایش «جوکر»، و گذشته ی ایشان است، و این شخصیت، از زوایای گوناگون از جمله روان‌شناسی، مورد بررسی قرار می‌گیرد؛ در «شوخی مرگبار»، «جوکر» به عنوان یک کمدین شکست‌ خورده توصیف شده، که پس از رسیدن به مرز جنون، وارد مبارزه با «گاتهام» شده، و «بتمن» به همراه «کمیسر گوردون»، کوشش برای متوقف کردن او دارند؛ <br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 26/04/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2231463573?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fabian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fabian" href="/user/show/1036893-fabian">Fabian</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1852954503384078894">The Killing Joke does much more for the iconic symbolism & stylistic edge of the Batman mythology than the serious-as-a-heart attack (overrated) Christopher Nolan films. But I am admittedly really in no position to analyze,* I leave this to the millions and lkegions of fans. The afterward by maestro illustrator**- his representation the most demonic and therefore probably my favorite interpretation of the Joker--is correct when he says that Alan Moore has written better stuff. (Watchmen, From He</span>
  <span id="freeText1852954503384078894" style="display:none">The Killing Joke does much more for the iconic symbolism &amp; stylistic edge of the Batman mythology than the serious-as-a-heart attack (overrated) Christopher Nolan films. But I am admittedly really in no position to analyze,* I leave this to the millions and lkegions of fans. The afterward by maestro illustrator**- his representation the most demonic and therefore probably my favorite interpretation of the Joker--is correct when he says that Alan Moore has written better stuff. (Watchmen, From Hell, even Fashion Beast...)<br /><br />* Well, I will say I do have the fondest memories of the fox animated series-the Mad Hatter being my favorite (underutilized) villain.<br /><br />** This cover is probably as iconographic as Edvard Munch's 'The Scream' at this point.</span>

<div id="review_739341877" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/739341877" />
    <a title="Jeff " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12618229-jeff"><img alt="Jeff " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529089518p2/12618229.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/739341877?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeff " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeff " href="/user/show/12618229-jeff">Jeff </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781401216672" href="/book/show/2233549.Batman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12618229-jeff?shelf=comix">comix</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer739341877" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer253775612871119762">Should some origin stories be better left untold? <br/><br/>Comic publishers will embellish the backstory of character more than necessary or drag it out and milk it, or they’ll retcon the character one too many times until the reader doesn’t know which way is up. If there’s a month, a week, a day, a couple of minutes left undocumented in a character’s background, it’ll be fodder for a future story.<br/><br/>Does the Joker need an origin story? <br/><br/>Some basic facts are presented here: He was once “normal”. He became a </span>
  <span id="freeText253775612871119762" style="display:none">Should some origin stories be better left untold? <br><br>Comic publishers will embellish the backstory of character more than necessary or drag it out and milk it, or they’ll retcon the character one too many times until the reader doesn’t know which way is up. If there’s a month, a week, a day, a couple of minutes left undocumented in a character’s background, it’ll be fodder for a future story.<br><br>Does the Joker need an origin story? <br><br>Some basic facts are presented here: He was once “normal”. He became a small time criminal out of necessity. He inadvertently gets dumped into a vat of <s>Kool-Ade</s> chemicals by Batman. As a result, he goes stark, raving bonkers.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452098065i/17646788._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>How much more of the Joker’s backstory do we want to be privy to? Do we need to add the fact that he was a struggling stand-up comedian and had a pregnant wife to the mix? Is sympathy necessary to appreciate and like the character even more? <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452098065i/17646789._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Joker’s persona is established as a homicidal loon, but do we have to be there at square one? Can his “accident” really turn him from an ordinary guy to a criminal mastermind, divorced of all humanity? Can the collective comic reader brain fill in the blanks themselves, leaving something to the imagination and not have it spoon fed to us? Do we need the complete story?<br><br>Back in the ‘80’s, before the ‘90’s when collectors nearly killed off the industry (Psst. Hey mister, you wanna buy a truckload of alternate foil #1 issues of Spider-Man 2099?), comic book creators were expanding the kiddie-geared bounds of storytelling by getting edgy and no one was more on board with the movement to more mature themes than Alan Moore, hence his interest in the Joker’s story.<br><br>This isn’t a Batman book. Bats comes off as weak, conciliatory, a step behind the Joker, his arch-nemesis. Sure I get the oft presented theory that they’re two parts to a whole, ying to the yang, “you complete me”, “let’s stop the madness, because one of us is going to die” yada, yada, yada… Here, Batman is a second banana.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452098065i/17646790._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Joker even gets the better of Batman in combat! More than once!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452098065i/17646791._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>C’mon Bats, you didn’t see that coming with your ninja skillz and training?</i><br><br>Brian Bolland’s art is exceptional and sells the story far better than Moore’s writing. That said, this a graphic novel that fans of Batman and the super hero genre should check out, if they haven’t done so already. It’s a defining moment in the Batman family legend and a game changer for Barbara Gordon -&gt; Batgirl -&gt; Oracle.<br><br><b>Bottom line</b>: This book has some panels that will be burned into your brain for the rest of your life. The Joker shooting Barbara Gordon usually makes top five lists of most memorable comic moments. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452098065i/17646792.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Seeing Commissioner Gordon trussed up naked and led around an abandoned amusement park by creepy, deranged midgets and driven to the edge of insanity is something I’d like to mind wipe.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452098417i/17646908.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>“Top of the pile of dolls, Ma!!”<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="253775612871119762" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer1129200193968472562">MY BLOG: <a href='http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/03/batman-killing-joke-by-alan-more-brian.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Melissa Martin's Reading List</a><br/><br/><b>OMG! THIS BOOK WAS AWESOME! THE STORY LINE! THE GRAPHICS ARE FREAKING AMAZING!</b><br/><br/>I'm sure everyone and their cousin has already read this book, but I haven't so here we go. This is about how the joker turned nutsy cuckoo! He had a good job but left it thinking he could be a stand up comedian and support his wife and unborn baby. Well.... that didn't happen, he apparently wasn't funny --->who knew?<br/><br/>Then he goes and tries to get some crime job with some idiots so </span>
  <span id="freeText1129200193968472562" style="display:none">MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/03/batman-killing-joke-by-alan-more-brian.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a><br><br><b>OMG! THIS BOOK WAS AWESOME! THE STORY LINE! THE GRAPHICS ARE FREAKING AMAZING!</b><br><br>I'm sure everyone and their cousin has already read this book, but I haven't so here we go. This is about how the joker turned nutsy cuckoo! He had a good job but left it thinking he could be a stand up comedian and support his wife and unborn baby. Well.... that didn't happen, he apparently wasn't funny ---&gt;who knew?<br><br>Then he goes and tries to get some crime job with some idiots so he could have the money until he could figure something out. Being out in a warehouse with said "idiots".. he has some stupid mask on, they get chased by security, he falls in some chemical crap and comes out whackadoo. I think it's brilliant. <br><br>Then he goes and shoots batgirl, kidnaps the commissioner and puts him in some freak show at a carnival he bought (or stole). It's just all so freaky and cool! I'm going to leave it at that and close with some awesome graphics! :-)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457209755i/18334326._SY540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457209755i/18334327._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457209755i/18334328._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457209755i/18334329._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My favorite is when they are laughing at his joke in the picture above ↑ :-D<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457209755i/18334330._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>We are all mad here! <div id="review_365790164" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/365790164" />
    <a title="Ronyell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell"><img alt="Ronyell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506581787p2/1169488.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/365790164?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ronyell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ronyell" href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell">Ronyell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of The Joker!!!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=sexy-bad-boy-hero">sexy-bad-boy-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=modern-age-comics">modern-age-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=strong-hero">strong-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=strong-heroine">strong-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=my-blog-reviews">my-blog-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=alan-moore">alan-moore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=dc-comics">dc-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=graphic-novels-comics">graphic-novels-comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer365790164" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15227958948905081126"><b>
  <i>5.5 stars!!!</i>
</b><br/><br/><b>OH…MY…GOD…</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380383566i/741790.jpg' width='480' height='365' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>I thought I knew everything there was to know about the Joker, one of Batman’s greatest foes. But after reading “Batman: The Killing Joke” and how the Joker was portrayed in this book, the Joker has officially become one of the most <b>VILE, TWISTED, DARK and most DISTURBING</b> villain I have ever come face to face with…<b>AND I LOVED IT!</b> Being brilliantly written by Alan Moore and being masterfully illustrated by Brian Bolland, “Batman: The Killing Joke” has remained to be one</span>
  <span id="freeText15227958948905081126" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>5.5 stars!!!</i>
</b><br><br><b>OH…MY…GOD…</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380383566i/741790.jpg" width="480" height="365" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I thought I knew everything there was to know about the Joker, one of Batman’s greatest foes. But after reading “Batman: The Killing Joke” and how the Joker was portrayed in this book, the Joker has officially become one of the most <b>VILE, TWISTED, DARK and most DISTURBING</b> villain I have ever come face to face with…<b>AND I LOVED IT!</b> Being brilliantly written by Alan Moore and being masterfully illustrated by Brian Bolland, “Batman: The Killing Joke” has remained to be one of the greatest and most disturbing “Batman” stories to ever be created!<br><br><b>
  <u>What is the story?</u>
</b> <br><br>When it turns out that the Joker, one of Batman’s greatest foes, breaks out of Arkham Asylum, Batman must stop this evil doer at all costs. Unfortunately, the Joker then comes after Commissioner Gordon and his daughter Barbara and performs some of the most vile and disturbing acts in his villainous career (starts by shooting Barbara Gordon, paralyzing her and then twisting Commissioner Gordon’s mind to make him crazy) and Batman must stop the Joker before it is too late. Also, we are introduced to the back story of the Joker and how he became the villain he is known as today. <br><br><b>
  <u>What I loved about this comic:</u>
</b><br><br><u>Alan Moore’s writing:</u> <b>WOW!</b> I mean, I thought that I have read some of the best Batman stories around (“Batman: Year One” for starters), but I think that “Batman: The Killing Joke” has nearly beaten some of the best “Batman” stories I had read! I had read some of Alan Moore’s works (The League of Extraordinary Gentlemen), but I can easily say that this graphic novel is easily one of his best works! I loved the way that Alan Moore made this story extremely disturbing and dark and I was actually cringing during the scene where Barbara Gordon is shot and then tortured, which proved how demented the Joker really is. I also loved the way that Alan Moore portrayed the relationship between Batman and the Joker since it is rare that I see a hero and a villain have a sort of understandable relationship seeing as how they both had lost people dear to them, but viewed life in a different life. I enjoyed the psychological message that Alan Moore was presenting in this story as the Joker sees life as being a huge awful joke (meaning that life is miserable) while Batman is truly trying to see the reality of the situations in life. I really enjoyed seeing the back story of the Joker as we learn what he was like before he became the villain he is known today and that really added so much depth to the story and to the character of the Joker. The ending of this story was truly terrifying yet amazing to see at the same time (I will not spoil it for you, but let us just say it is the confrontation between Batman and the Joker).<br><br><u>Brian Bolland’s artwork:</u> Brian Bolland had done a truly amazing job at providing the artwork of this story as all the characters look truly realistic and colorful. I loved the attention in details that Brian Bolland gives to the characters’ facial expressions, especially the Joker as he is seen smiling dementedly, which makes him a truly menacing character to look at. My favorite artwork in this graphic novel was of the images of the rain drops making small circles in the ground, as they look truly beautiful and yet give this story a truly ominous feel as these images appear at the beginning of the book towards the end of the book.<br><br><b>
  <u>What made me feel uncomfortable about this book:</u>
</b> <br><br>The only issue with this graphic novel that some readers would have problems with is the fact that the story is extremely dark and disturbing for your average “Batman” story. For one thing, there is a scene where Barbara Gordon is shot and then tortured which would disturb many readers (it definitely disturbed me a bit). Also, as in many “Batman” stories, the atmosphere of this story is extremely dark and brooding and that might be a bit uncomfortable for many readers who are not used to reading dark stories to handle.<br><br><b>
  <u>Final Thoughts:</u>
</b><br><br>So what is my final verdict on this story? “Batman: The Killing Joke” is easily one of the most disturbing yet most amazing stories I have ever read and I would <b>HIGHLY RECOMMEND</b> this story to “Batman” fans everywhere who love a good dark and intelligent story about the follies of life.<br><br><b>Review is also on: <a href="http://rabbitearsbookblog.blogspot.com/2012/07/batman-killing-joke-by-alan-moore.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabbit Ears Book Blog</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="15227958948905081126" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Not only did they become some of my favourite films of all time, but they also gave me one of my favourite villains of all time: <b>The Joker.</b><br/><br/>And I figured it was about damn time I took a leap into where it all actually began– the comics.<br/><br/>There's no doubt that this green-haired madman is universally hailed as perhaps the best antagonist to have ever been created, and one can </span>
  <span id="freeText2963304360152637682" style="display:none">An accurate depiction of what these 45 minutes felt like:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481028410ra/21375803.gif" width="320" height="320" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Nolan's movies are the reason I got hooked into the world of Batman. Not only did they become some of my favourite films of all time, but they also gave me one of my favourite villains of all time: <b>The Joker.</b><br><br>And I figured it was about damn time I took a leap into where it all actually began– the comics.<br><br>There's no doubt that this green-haired madman is universally hailed as perhaps the best antagonist to have ever been created, and one can easily see why that is. <i>The Killing Joke</i> presents us with his backstory: a deeper insight into the man the Joker once was, and the events that led to the loss of his sanity. <br><br>Whether or not you like the inclusion of this origin is entirely subjective but as for me, I feel like it only further added to this brilliant criminal mastermind's many layers and complexities (and dare I say it, even a strong sense of sympathy). <br><br>The story centrally revolves around the Joker's sadistic quest to prove that all it takes is "one bad day" for a person to lose their mind, whilst flickering between flashbacks and current events, using <i>beautifully</i> done match-cut techniques. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[

 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>More than that, this graphic novel showcased some incredibly smart dialogue, iconic Batman moments and commendable artwork from Brian Bolland. And can I just say how <i>pleased</i> I am at his decision to recolour the deluxe version? It does wonders in setting the right, creepy atmosphere, just take a look!<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[

<div id="review_1767636909" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1767636909" />
    <a title="Tim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7202176-tim"><img alt="Tim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1324164999p2/7202176.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1767636909?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tim" href="/user/show/7202176-tim">Tim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7202176-tim?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1767636909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6593556532914365167">This is not the perfect Batman story. It’s got several weird choices, some extremely offensive moments and one of the most infamous scenes of violence towards a female character in comic history (story goes that when Moore mentioned the idea of damaging Barbara Gordon’s spine, the higher ups at DC responded to him with “Fine, cripple the bitch”). Flaws aside, it is the perfect Joker story.<br/><br/>These random acts of violence, these weird choices and offensive mockeries… they fit the Joker’s twisted sen</span>
  <span id="freeText6593556532914365167" style="display:none">This is not the perfect Batman story. It’s got several weird choices, some extremely offensive moments and one of the most infamous scenes of violence towards a female character in comic history (story goes that when Moore mentioned the idea of damaging Barbara Gordon’s spine, the higher ups at DC responded to him with “Fine, cripple the bitch”). Flaws aside, it is the perfect Joker story.<br><br>These random acts of violence, these weird choices and offensive mockeries… they fit the Joker’s twisted sense of humor. It shows him at his cruelest.<br><br>It also shows him at his most sympathetic.<br><br>Alan Moore took his considerable talents and applied it to reworking the Joker’s backstory; to making it absolutely depressing and then adding in the element that the Joker himself is not even sure if it's correct. What’s important is that he believes it… at least at the time. <br><br>The artwork is stunning (especially in the recolored version that is currently in print) and shows the Joker, while almost always grinning, always with sad eyes. I mean seriously, just look at him.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1589572737i/29483093._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1589572737i/29483094._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1577709049i/28688494._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>This is one of those comics that needs to be experienced. I could go on at length, but could never do it justice. My suggestion is to just check it out for yourself.<br><br>Let me close though with the Joker’s monologue. It’s long, but says more about his character than I ever could, and is one of the best written I’ve ever seen in a comic.<br><br>"So... I see you received the free ticket I sent you. I'm glad. I did so want you to be here. You see it doesn't matter if you catch me and send me back to the asylum... Gordon's been driven mad. I've proved my point. I've demonstrated there's no difference between me and everyone else! All it takes is one bad day to reduce the sanest man alive to lunacy. That's how far the world is from where I am. Just one bad day. You had a bad day once, am I right? I know I am. I can tell. You had a bad day and everything changed. Why else would you dress up as a flying rat? You had a bad day, and it drove you as crazy as everybody else... Only you won't admit it! You have to keep pretending that life makes sense, that there's some point to all this struggling! God you make me want to puke. I mean, what is it with you? What made you what you are? Girlfriend killed by the mob, maybe? Brother carved up by some mugger? Something like that, I bet. Something like that... Something like that happened to me, you know. I... I'm not exactly sure what it was. Sometimes I remember it one way, sometimes another... If I'm going to have a past, I prefer it to be multiple choice! Ha ha ha! But my point is... My point is, I went crazy. When I saw what a black, awful joke the world was, I went crazy as a coot! I admit it! Why can't you? I mean, you're not unintelligent! You must see the reality of the situation. Do you know how many times we've come close to world war three over a flock of geese on a computer screen? Do you know what triggered the last world war? An argument over how many telegraph poles Germany owed its war debt creditors! Telegraph poles! Ha ha ha ha HA! It's all a joke! Everything anybody ever valued or struggled for... it's all a monstrous, demented gag! So why can't you see the funny side? Why aren't you laughing?"<br><br>5/5 stars<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="6593556532914365167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1364366347" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1364366347" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7477266-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1433820623p2/7477266.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1364366347?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/7477266-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18675939-batman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7477266-sarah?shelf=z2015">z2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7477266-sarah?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7477266-sarah?shelf=z2018">z2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7477266-sarah?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7477266-sarah?shelf=books-i-ve-read-more-than-once">books-i-ve-read-more-than-once</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1364366347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4326243498561265609">Just finished rereading this. It’s still such a cool comic! <br/><br/>*Batman voice* "WHERE IS HE?" <br/><br/>I can see why this is so popular. The story is great and the illustrations are phenomenal. I love the Joker, he's my favourite batman villain (and possibly my all-time favourite comic/superhero villain too). He is just completely insane and I love it. <br/><br/>I love getting backstories so I loved getting to see an adaptation of why the Joker was the way he was. It was really well done. However, after reading this I</span>
  <span id="freeText4326243498561265609" style="display:none">Just finished rereading this. It’s still such a cool comic! <br /><br />*Batman voice* "WHERE IS HE?" <br /><br />I can see why this is so popular. The story is great and the illustrations are phenomenal. I love the Joker, he's my favourite batman villain (and possibly my all-time favourite comic/superhero villain too). He is just completely insane and I love it. <br /><br />I love getting backstories so I loved getting to see an adaptation of why the Joker was the way he was. It was really well done. However, after reading this I felt a little conflicted. One big reason why I love the Joker is because he is quite mysterious. He's insane and because you don't know why, it makes him scarier. So Moore wrote this great back story BUT part of me wasn't really completely satisfied. I only realised after I read this, that the mystery was a big issue for me. <br /><br />Batman was such a douche in this (even more than usual). I love Batman but I don't think Moore wrote him as a very likeable character. I actually liked the ending a lot. I was smiling because I thought it was sweet. I know the ending is ambiguous and open to interpretation but I consider it a happy ending. This comic was actually quite philosophical. I kept reading things that reminded me of different philosophers I've studied. I especially liked the Joker's speech about insanity and reason. <br /><br />THE BEST thing about this was 100% the artwork. It is absolutely beautiful. It's crisp, clean, very detailed and the colours are just perfect. I was fangirling at how great the art was in every single panel. Brian Bollard is brilliant.<br /><br />I would recommend this and I'll definitely be reading more from Moore and Bollard.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4326243498561265609" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5057646040512769778"><blockquote><b><i>"All it takes is one bad day to reduce the sanest man alive to lunacy."</i></b>--Joker</blockquote>Wow! It's good! I liked this comic. I admit I was afraid because I thought it was published in 1988 and the work of graphics wouldn't be good. But at the same time I wanted to know the origin of Joker. The Joker in this one was portrayed better than that in The Man Who Laughs. <br/>The origin of Joker is heart breaking and pretty typical for o</span>
  <span id="freeText5057646040512769778" style="display:none"><blockquote><b><i>"All it takes is one bad day to reduce the sanest man alive to lunacy."</i></b>--Joker</blockquote>Wow! It's good! I liked this comic. I admit I was afraid because I thought it was published in 1988 and the work of graphics wouldn't be good. But at the same time I wanted to know the origin of Joker. In spite of its release date, the graphics were quite good. I enjoyed reading it. The Joker in this one was portrayed better than that in The Man Who Laughs. <br />The origin of Joker is heart breaking and pretty typical for our time. I didn't know about him much before this comic. Now I know there is one similarity between Batman and Joker. They both faced ONE bad day in the past. And THAT day determined their personality. The only difference between them is of the choice they made.<br />Now I have read both of their origin. They are good. Now I can read Batman comics without getting much hurdles. <br /><br />One more thing. Am I the only one who faced little problem with the ending? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[How it makes sense that Batman grabs the Joker and BAMM! <span id="freeTextContainer9759326418674414391"><i>English review at the bottom</i><br/><br/>¿Que puedo decir de esta historia que no se haya dicho ya? ¿Qué es un obra maestra? (y</span>
  <span id="freeText9759326418674414391" style="display:none"><i>English review at the bottom</i><br><br>¿Que puedo decir de esta historia que no se haya dicho ya? ¿Qué es un obra maestra? Lo es, el dialogo es increíble, la deconstrucción del Joker también, pocas historias nos han mostrado tantas capas de este personaje ¿Porqué? Fácil, tenemos su parte más vulnerable, una que pocas veces se había explotado, también tenemos al clásico Joker,al que, como diría Alfred, "Quiere ver arder al mundo"...pero hay otra capa, la que poco se atreven a mostrar y es ¿Porque Batman? (y por favor no digan que porque es el otro enmascarado) en respuesta a esa pregunta las últimas dos páginas las ame...<br><br>La manera en que Alan Moore lleva esta historia es fantastica porque sí, tiene su sello, el personaje tiene profundidad, pierde ese velo de idealización que ha cubierto al Joker desde hace años...y el dibujo es ideal.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447295929i/16983029._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447295929i/16983030._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>_____________________________________________<br><br>What can I say about this story that has not already been said? That is a masterpiece? It is, dialogue is amazing, the deconstruction of the Joker too, few stories have shown us so many layers of this character Why? Easy, we have his underbelly, one that rarely had exploded, we also have the classic Joker, who, like Alfred would say, "Wants to see the world burn" ... but there is another layer, which few people dare to show and it is, Why Batman? (And please don't say "because it is the other masked") in response to that question the last two pages are the most georgeous thing ...<br><br>The way that Alan Moore takes this story is fantastic because yes, has its stamp, the character has depth, it loses that veil of idealization that has covered the Joker for years ... and the drawing is ideal.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9759326418674414391" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2091567695" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2091567695" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi The Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi The Reader" href="/user/show/7986781-heidi-the-reader">Heidi The Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7986781-heidi-the-reader?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2091567695" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10101950002851574741">I've decided to explore the world of superhero comics. First on my list, <i>Batman: The Killing Joke</i> by Alan Moore.<br/><br/>The story opens on a dark and stormy night. We're heading into Arkham Asylum with Batman. After passing a few famous inmates, we're outside inmate #0801, Name Unknown's cell.<br/><br/>A shadowy figure is playing solitaire within the barred room. It's The Joker.<br/><br/>By far, one of the creepiest villains of the Batman pantheon.<br/><br/><i>"So when you find yourself locked onto an unpleasant train of thought, headi</i></span>
  <span id="freeText10101950002851574741" style="display:none">I've decided to explore the world of superhero comics. First on my list, <i>Batman: The Killing Joke</i> by Alan Moore.<br /><br />The story opens on a dark and stormy night. We're heading into Arkham Asylum with Batman. After passing a few famous inmates, we're outside inmate #0801, Name Unknown's cell.<br /><br />A shadowy figure is playing solitaire within the barred room. It's The Joker.<br /><br />By far, one of the creepiest villains of the Batman pantheon.<br /><br /><i>"So when you find yourself locked onto an unpleasant train of thought, heading for the places in your past where the screaming is unbearable, remember there's always madness. Madness is the emergency exit..."</i><br /><br />He is mad, yes, but brilliant in his insanity. And, in that, is he so different from the rest of the human race?<br /><br /><i>"Faced with the inescapable fact that human existence is mad, random and pointless, one in eight of them crack up and go stark slavering buggo! Who can blame them? In a world as psychotic as this... any other response would be crazy!"</i><br /><br />Recommended for the more mature graphic novel readers because of some disturbing content and images, <i>Batman: The Killing Joke</i> is no joke and one heck of a ride.<br /><br /><i>Watchmen</i>, also by Alan Moore, is one of my all time favorite graphic novels, so I was expecting to enjoy this one. If you haven't had a chance to read it yet, it's another must-read for the graphic novel fan.</span>
